   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg/260px-Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg/390px-Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg/520px-Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4402" data-file-height="2879"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Coupe_Davis_Finale_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2018 Davis Cup Final - opening ceremony
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <b>Davis Cup</b> is the premier international team event in men's <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>. It is run by the <a href="/wiki/International_Tennis_Federation" title="International Tennis Federation">International Tennis Federation</a> (ITF) and is contested annually between teams from competing countries in a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knock-out</a> format. It is described by the organisers as the "World Cup of Tennis", and the winners are referred to as the World Champion team.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The competition began in <a href="/wiki/1900_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1900 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1900</a> as a challenge between <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Davis_Cup_team" title="Great Britain Davis Cup team">Great Britain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Davis_Cup_team" title="United States Davis Cup team">United States</a>. By <a href="/wiki/2016_Davis_Cup" title="2016 Davis Cup">2016</a>, 135 nations entered teams into the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The most successful countries over the history of the tournament are the United States (winning 32 tournaments and finishing as runners-up 29 times) and <a href="/wiki/Australia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australia Davis Cup team">Australia</a> (winning 28 times, including four occasions with <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Davis_Cup_team" title="New Zealand Davis Cup team">New Zealand</a> as <a href="/wiki/Australasia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australasia Davis Cup team">Australasia</a>, and finishing as runners-up 19 times). The present champions are <a href="/wiki/Croatia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Croatia Davis Cup team">Croatia</a>, who beat <a href="/wiki/France_Davis_Cup_team" title="France Davis Cup team">France</a> to win their second title in 2018. </p>
      <p>The women's equivalent of the Davis Cup is the <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">Fed Cup</a>. Australia, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_Davis_Cup_team" title="Czech Republic Davis Cup team">Czech Republic</a>, and the United States are the only countries to have held both Davis Cup and Fed Cup titles in the same year. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg/220px-Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg/330px-Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg/440px-Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2403" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Davis_Cup_Praha_%C4%8CRo_2012-11-28_cropped_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Davis Cup
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The idea for a tournament pitting the best British and Americans in competition against one another was probably first conceived by <a href="/wiki/James_Dwight" title="James Dwight">James Dwight</a>, the first president of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Lawn_Tennis_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Lawn Tennis Association">U.S. National Lawn Tennis Association</a> when it formed in 1881. Desperate to assess the development of American players against the renowned British champions, he worked tirelessly to engage British officials in a properly sanctioned match, but failed to do so. He nevertheless tried to entice top international (particularly British) talent to the U.S. and sanctioned semi-official tours of the top American players to Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Diplomatic relations between Great Britain and the United Stated on the tennis front had strengthened such that, by the mid 1890s, reciprocal tours were staged annually between players of the two nations, and an ensuing friendship between American <a href="/wiki/William_Larned" title="William Larned">William Larned</a> and Irishman <a href="/wiki/Harold_Mahony" title="Harold Mahony">Harold Mahony</a> spurred efforts to formalize an official team competition between the two nations.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>International competitions had been staged for some time before the first Davis Cup match in 1900. From 1892, England and Ireland had been competing in an annual national-team-based competition, similar to what would become the standard Davis Cup format, mixing single and doubles matches, and in 1895 England played against France in a national team competition.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> During Larned's tour of the British Isles in 1896, where he competed in several tournaments including the <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon Championships</a>, he was also a spectator for the annual England vs. Ireland match. He returned to exclaim that Britain had agreed to send a group of three to the US the following summer, which would represent the first British lawn tennis "team" to compete in the U.S. Coincidentally, some weeks before Larned left for his British tour, the idea for an international competition was discussed also between leading figures in American lawn tennis - one of whom was tennis journalist E.P. Fischer - at a tournament in <a href="/wiki/Niagara-on-the-Lake" title="Niagara-on-the-Lake">Niagara-on-the-Lake</a>, Ontario. <a href="/wiki/Dwight_F._Davis" title="Dwight F. Davis">Dwight F. Davis</a> was in attendance at this tournament, and was thought to have got wind of the idea as it was discussed in the tournament's popular magazine, and Davis's name was mentioned as someone who might 'do something for the game … put up some big prize, or cup'.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Larned and Fischer met on several occasions that summer and discussed the idea of an international match to be held in Chicago the following summer, pitting six of the best British players against six of the best Americans, in a mixture of singles and doubles matches. This was discussed openly in two articles in the <i>Chicago Tribune</i>, but did not come to fruition.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nevertheless, the following summer, Great Britain - though not under the official auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Lawn_Tennis_Association" title="Lawn Tennis Association">Lawn Tennis Association</a> - sent three of its best players to compete in several US tournaments. Their relative poor performances convinced Dwight and other leading officials and figures in American lawn tennis that the time was right for a properly sanctioned international competition. This was to be staged in Newcastle in July 1898,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> but the event never took place as the Americans could not field a sufficiently strong team. A reciprocal tour to the U.S. in 1899 amounted to just a single British player travelling overseas, as many of the players were involved in overseas armed conflicts. </p>
      <p>It was at this juncture, in the summer of 1899, that four members of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> tennis team - Dwight Davis included - travelled across the States to challenge the best west-coast talent, and upon his return, it apparently occurred to Davis that if teams representing regions could arouse such great feelings, then why wouldn't a tennis event that pitted national teams in competition be just as successful. He approached James Dwight with the idea, which was tentatively agreed, and he ordered an appropriate <a href="/wiki/Sterling_silver" title="Sterling silver">sterling silver</a> punchbowl trophy from <a href="/wiki/Shreve,_Crump_%26_Low" title="Shreve, Crump &amp; Low">Shreve, Crump &amp; Low</a>, purchasing it from his own funds for about <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>1,000.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> They in turn commissioned a classically styled design from <a href="/wiki/William_B._Durgin_Company" title="William B. Durgin Company">William B. Durgin</a>'s of <a href="/wiki/Concord,_New_Hampshire" title="Concord, New Hampshire">Concord, New Hampshire</a>, crafted by the Englishman <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rowland_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rowland Rhodes (page does not exist)">Rowland Rhodes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-maker_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maker-11">[11]</a></sup> Beyond donating a trophy for the competition, however, Davis's involvement in the incipient development of the tournament that came to bear his name was negligible, yet a persistent myth has emerged that Davis devised both the idea for an international tennis competition and its format of mixing singles and doubles matches. Research has shown this to be a myth,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> similar in its exaggeration of a single individual's efforts within a highly complex long-term development to the myths of <a href="/wiki/William_Webb_Ellis" title="William Webb Ellis">William Webb Ellis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abner_Doubleday" title="Abner Doubleday">Abner Doubleday</a>, who have both been wrongly credited with inventing rugby and baseball, respectively. Davis nevertheless went on to become a prominent politician in the United States in the 1920s, serving as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War" title="United States Secretary of War">US Secretary of War</a> from 1925 to 1929 and as <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">Governor-General</a> of the Philippines from 1929 to 1932. </p>
      <p>The first match, between the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Davis_Cup_team" title="United States Davis Cup team">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Davis_Cup_team" title="Great Britain Davis Cup team">Britain</a> (competing as the "British Isles"), was held at the <a href="/wiki/Longwood_Cricket_Club" title="Longwood Cricket Club">Longwood Cricket Club</a> in Boston, Massachusetts in <a href="/wiki/1900_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1900 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1900</a>. The American team, of which Dwight Davis was a part, surprised the British by winning the first three matches. The following year the two countries did not compete, but the US won the match in <a href="/wiki/1902_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1902 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1902</a> and Britain won the following four matches. By <a href="/wiki/1905_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1905 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1905</a> the tournament expanded to include <a href="/wiki/Belgium_Davis_Cup_team" title="Belgium Davis Cup team">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria_Davis_Cup_team" title="Austria Davis Cup team">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_Davis_Cup_team" title="France Davis Cup team">France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Australasia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australasia Davis Cup team">Australasia</a>, a combined team from Australia and New Zealand that competed together until <a href="/wiki/1914_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1914 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1914</a>. </p>
      <p>The tournament was initially titled the <i>International Lawn Tennis Challenge</i> although it soon became known as the <i>Davis Cup</i>, after Dwight Davis' trophy. The Davis Cup competition was initially played as a <a href="/wiki/Tournament#Challenge" title="Tournament">challenge</a> cup. All teams competed against one another for the right to face the previous year's champion in the final round. </p>
      <p>Beginning in <a href="/wiki/1923_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1923 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1923</a>, the world's teams were split into two zones: the "America Zone" and the "Europe Zone". The winners of the two zones met in the <i>Inter-Zonal Zone</i> ("INZ") to decide which national team would challenge the defending champion for the cup. In <a href="/wiki/1955_Davis_Cup" title="1955 Davis Cup">1955</a> a third zone, the "Eastern Zone", was added. Because there were three zones, the winner of one of the three zones received a bye in the first round of the INZ challenger rounds. In <a href="/wiki/1966_Davis_Cup" title="1966 Davis Cup">1966</a>, the "Europe Zone" was split into two zones, "Europe Zone A" and "Europe Zone B", so the winners of the four zones competed in the INZ challenger rounds. </p>
      <p>From <a href="/wiki/1950_Davis_Cup" title="1950 Davis Cup">1950</a> to <a href="/wiki/1967_Davis_Cup" title="1967 Davis Cup">1967</a>, Australia dominated the competition, winning the Cup 15 times in 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Beginning in <a href="/wiki/1972_Davis_Cup" title="1972 Davis Cup">1972</a>, the format was changed to a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout tournament</a>, so that the defending champion was required to compete in all rounds, and the Davis Cup was awarded to the tournament champion. </p>
      <p>Up until <a href="/wiki/1973_Davis_Cup" title="1973 Davis Cup">1973</a>, the Davis Cup had only ever been won by the United States, Great Britain/British Isles, France and Australia/Australasia. Their domination was eventually broken in <a href="/wiki/1974_Davis_Cup" title="1974 Davis Cup">1974</a> when <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_Davis_Cup_team" title="South Africa Davis Cup team">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/India_Davis_Cup_team" title="India Davis Cup team">India</a> made the final; however the final was scratched and South Africa awarded the cup after India <a href="/wiki/Sporting_boycott_of_South_Africa_during_the_apartheid_era" title="Sporting boycott of South Africa during the apartheid era">refused to travel to South Africa</a> in protest of South Africa's <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> policies. <a href="/wiki/1975_Davis_Cup" title="1975 Davis Cup">The following year</a> saw the first actual final between two "outsider" nations, when <a href="/wiki/Sweden_Davis_Cup_team" title="Sweden Davis Cup team">Sweden</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Czechoslovakia Davis Cup team">Czechoslovakia</a> 3–2, and since then, many other countries have gone on to capture the trophy. </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/1981_Davis_Cup" title="1981 Davis Cup">1981</a>, a tiered system of competition was created, in which the 16 best national teams compete in the <i>World Group</i> and all other national teams compete in one of four groups in one of three regional zones. In <a href="/wiki/1989_Davis_Cup" title="1989 Davis Cup">1989</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tiebreak_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiebreak (tennis)">tiebreak</a> was introduced into Davis Cup competition, and from <a href="/wiki/2016_Davis_Cup" title="2016 Davis Cup">2016</a> it is used in all five sets.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, the ITF voted to change the format of the competition from 2019 onwards, changing it to an 18-team event to happen at the end of the season, with 71% of ITF member federations voting in favour of the change. The new format, backed by footballer <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Pique" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerard Pique">Gerard Pique</a> and Japanese businessman <a href="/wiki/Hiroshi_Mikitani" title="Hiroshi Mikitani">Hiroshi Mikitani</a>, was likened to a world cup of tennis and was designed to be more attractive to sponsors and broadcasters. Opposing federations included those from Australia, Germany, and Great Britain. Support for the reform was also mixed among current and former players, with some such as <a href="/wiki/Novak_Djokovic" title="Novak Djokovic">Novak Djokovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Nadal" title="Rafael Nadal">Rafael Nadal</a> being in favour of the new format, but others such as <a href="/wiki/Rod_Laver" title="Rod Laver">Rod Laver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Pouille" title="Lucas Pouille">Lucas Pouille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> being opposed.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Davis Cup games have been affected by political protests several times, especially in Sweden: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The match between Sweden and <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> 1968 was supposed to be played in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A5stad" title="Båstad">Båstad</a> but was moved to <a href="/wiki/Bandol" title="Bandol">Bandol</a>, France, due to protests against the Rhodesian <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia%27s_Unilateral_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Rhodesia's Unilateral Declaration of Independence">white minority government</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ian_Smith" title="Ian Smith">Ian Smith</a>.</li> 
       <li>The Swedish government tried to stop the match between <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and Sweden in 1975 in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A5stad" title="Båstad">Båstad</a>, due to violations of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> in Chile. The match was played, even while 7,000 people protested against it outside.</li> 
       <li>After the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict</a>, 6,000 people protested against Israel outside the <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malmö">Malmö</a> city Davis Cup match between Sweden and Israel in March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6_Municipality" title="Malmö Municipality">Malmö Municipality</a> politicians were concerned about extremists, and decided due to security reasons to only let a small audience in.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg/220px-Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg/330px-Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg/440px-Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Davis_Cup_Roland_Garros.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Monument to the Davis Cup at 
         <a href="/wiki/Stade_Roland_Garros" title="Stade Roland Garros">Stade Roland Garros</a> in Paris, France
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tournament">Tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 16 best national teams are assigned to the World Group and compete annually for the Davis Cup. Nations which are not in the World Group compete in one of three regional zones (Americas, Asia/Oceania, and Europe/Africa). The competition is spread over four weekends during the year. Each elimination round between competing nations is held in one of the countries, and is played as the best of five matches (4 singles, 1 doubles). The ITF determines the host countries for all possible matchups before each year's tournament. </p>
      <p>The World Group is the top group and includes the world's best 16 national teams. Teams in the World Group play a four-round elimination tournament. Teams are seeded based on a ranking system released by the ITF, taking into account previous years' results. The defending champion and runner-up are always the top two seeds in the tournament. The losers of the first-round matches are sent to the World Group playoff round, where they play along with winners from Group I of the regional zones. The playoff round winners play in the World Group for the next year's tournament, while the losers play in Group I of their respective regional zone. </p>
      <p>Each of the three regional zones is divided into four groups. Groups I and II play elimination rounds, with the losing teams facing relegation to the next-lower group. The teams in Groups III and those in Group IV play a <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin tournament</a> with promotion and relegation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <p>Note: The total number of nations in Group One is 24. However, the distribution among the three zones may vary each year, according to the number of nations promoted or relegated between Group One and the World Group. The number of nations in the World Group and Group One together is 22 from Euro/Africa Zone, 9 from Americas Zone and 9 from Asia/Oceania Zone. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ties_and_rubbers">Ties and rubbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ties and rubbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As in other cup competitions <i>tie</i> is used in the Davis Cup to mean an elimination round. In the Davis Cup, the word <i>rubber</i> means an individual match. </p>
      <p>In the annual World Group competition, 16 nations compete in eight first-round ties; the eight winners compete in four quarterfinal ties; the four winners compete in two semifinal ties; and the two winners compete in the final tie. </p>
      <p>Each tie consists of five rubbers, which are played in three days (usually on Friday, Saturday, and Sunday). The winner of the tie is the nation which wins three or more of the five rubbers in the tie. On the first day, the first two rubbers are <a href="/wiki/Singles_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="Singles (tennis)">singles</a>, which are generally played by each nation's two best available singles players. On the second day, the <a href="/wiki/Doubles_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doubles (tennis)">doubles</a> rubber is played. On the third day, the final two rubbers are typically <i>reverse singles</i>, in which the first-day contestants usually play again, but they swap opponents from the first day's singles rubbers. However, in certain circumstances, the team captain may replace one or two of the players who played the singles on Friday by other players who were nominated for the tie. For example, if the tie has already been decided in favour of one of the teams, it is common for younger or lower-ranked team members to play the remaining <i><a href="/wiki/Dead_rubber" title="Dead rubber">dead rubbers</a></i> in order for them to gain Davis Cup experience. </p>
      <p>Since 2011, if a nation has a winning 3–1 lead after the first reverse single match and that match has gone to four sets or more, then the remaining reverse single match which is a dead rubber is not played. All five rubbers are played if one nation has a winning 3–0 lead after the doubles match.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ties are played at a venue chosen by one of the competing countries. The right of choice is given on an alternating basis. Therefore, countries play in the country where the last tie between the teams was not held. In case the two countries have not met since 1970, lots are drawn to determine the host country.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Venues in the World Group must comply with certain minimum standards, including a minimum seating capacity as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>World Group play-offs: 4,000</li> 
       <li>World Group first round: 4,000</li> 
       <li>World Group quarterfinals: 6,000</li> 
       <li>World Group semifinals: 8,000</li> 
       <li>World Group final: 12,000</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Captain">Captain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Captain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Prior to each tie, the captain (non-playing coach appointed by the national association) nominates a squad of four players and decides who will compete in the tie. On the day before play starts, the order of play for the first day is drawn at random. In the past, teams could substitute final day singles players only in case of injury or illness, verified by a doctor, but current rules permit the captain to designate any player to play the last two singles rubbers, provided that no first day matchup is repeated. There is no restriction on which of the playing team members may play the doubles rubber: the two singles players, two other players (usually doubles specialists) or a combination. </p>
      <p>Each rubber is normally played as best of five <a href="/wiki/Tennis_score#Scoring_a_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennis score">sets</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/2016_Davis_Cup" title="2016 Davis Cup">2016</a>, all sets use a <a href="/wiki/Tiebreak_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiebreak (tennis)">tiebreak</a> at 6–6 if necessary (formerly, the fifth set usually had no tiebreaker, so play continued until one side won by two games e.g. 10–8). However, if a team has clinched the tie before all five rubbers have been completed, the remaining rubbers may be shortened to best of three sets, with a tiebreak if necessary to decide all three sets. </p>
      <p>In Group III and Group IV competitions, each tie consists only of three rubbers, which include two singles and one doubles rubber, which is played in a single day. The rubbers are in the best of three sets format, with a tie breaker if necessary to decide all three sets. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_statistics">Records and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Records and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_by_team">Performance by team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Performance by team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       <li><b>Consecutive titles</b> 
        <ul>
         <li>All-time: 7, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Davis_Cup_team" title="United States Davis Cup team">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/1920_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1920 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1920</a>–<a href="/wiki/1926_International_Lawn_Tennis_Challenge" title="1926 International Lawn Tennis Challenge">1926</a></li> 
         <li>Post-Challenge Round: 2; <a href="/wiki/United_States_Davis_Cup_team" title="United States Davis Cup team">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_Davis_Cup" title="1978 Davis Cup">1978</a>–<a href="/wiki/1979_Davis_Cup" title="1979 Davis Cup">79</a>, <a href="/wiki/1981_Davis_Cup" title="1981 Davis Cup">1981</a>–<a href="/wiki/1982_Davis_Cup" title="1982 Davis Cup">82</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sweden_Davis_Cup_team" title="Sweden Davis Cup team">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/1984_Davis_Cup" title="1984 Davis Cup">1984</a>–<a href="/wiki/1985_Davis_Cup" title="1985 Davis Cup">85</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_Davis_Cup" title="1997 Davis Cup">1997</a>–<a href="/wiki/1998_Davis_Cup" title="1998 Davis Cup">98</a>; <a href="/wiki/Germany_Davis_Cup_team" title="Germany Davis Cup team">West Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/1988_Davis_Cup" title="1988 Davis Cup">1988</a>–<a href="/wiki/1989_Davis_Cup" title="1989 Davis Cup">89</a>; <a href="/wiki/Spain_Davis_Cup_team" title="Spain Davis Cup team">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Davis_Cup" title="2008 Davis Cup">2008</a>–<a href="/wiki/2009_Davis_Cup" title="2009 Davis Cup">09</a>; <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_Davis_Cup_team" title="Czech Republic Davis Cup team">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Davis_Cup" title="2012 Davis Cup">2012</a>–<a href="/wiki/2013_Davis_Cup" title="2013 Davis Cup">13</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Consecutive finals appearances</b> 
        <ul>
         <li>All-time: 23, <a href="/wiki/Australia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australia Davis Cup team">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/1946_Davis_Cup" title="1946 Davis Cup">1946</a>–<a href="/wiki/1968_Davis_Cup" title="1968 Davis Cup">1968</a></li> 
         <li>Post-Challenge Round: 7, <a href="/wiki/Sweden_Davis_Cup_team" title="Sweden Davis Cup team">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/1983_Davis_Cup" title="1983 Davis Cup">1983</a>–<a href="/wiki/1989_Davis_Cup" title="1989 Davis Cup">1989</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most games in a tie</b> 
        <ul>
         <li>All-time: 327, <a href="/wiki/India_Davis_Cup_team" title="India Davis Cup team">India</a> 3–2 <a href="/wiki/Australia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australia Davis Cup team">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/1974_Davis_Cup" title="1974 Davis Cup">1974</a> Eastern Zone final</li> 
         <li>World Group (before tiebreak): 281, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_Davis_Cup_team" title="Paraguay Davis Cup team">Paraguay</a> 3–2 <a href="/wiki/France_Davis_Cup_team" title="France Davis Cup team">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985_Davis_Cup" title="1985 Davis Cup">1985</a> first round</li> 
         <li>World Group (since tiebreak): 281, <a href="/wiki/Romania_Davis_Cup_team" title="Romania Davis Cup team">Romania</a> 3–2 <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_Davis_Cup_team" title="Ecuador Davis Cup team">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_Davis_Cup" title="2003 Davis Cup">2003</a> World Group play-offs</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>Most titles as a player</b>; 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Roy_Emerson" title="Roy Emerson">Roy Emerson</a>; <a href="/wiki/Australia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australia Davis Cup team">Australia</a>; 8 titles (<a href="/wiki/1959_Davis_Cup" title="1959 Davis Cup">1959</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_Davis_Cup" title="1960 Davis Cup">1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961_Davis_Cup" title="1961 Davis Cup">1961</a>, <a href="/wiki/1962_Davis_Cup" title="1962 Davis Cup">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_Davis_Cup" title="1964 Davis Cup">1964</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965_Davis_Cup" title="1965 Davis Cup">1965</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_Davis_Cup" title="1966 Davis Cup">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_Davis_Cup" title="1967 Davis Cup">1967</a>)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most titles as captain</b>; 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Hopman" title="Harry Hopman">Harry Hopman</a>; <a href="/wiki/Australia_Davis_Cup_team" title="Australia Davis Cup team">Australia</a>; 16 titles (<a href="/wiki/1939_Davis_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1939 Davis Cup">1939</a>, <a href="/wiki/1950_Davis_Cup" title="1950 Davis Cup">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/1951_Davis_Cup" title="1951 Davis Cup">1951</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_Davis_Cup" title="1952 Davis Cup">1952</a>, <a href="/wiki/1953_Davis_Cup" title="1953 Davis Cup">1953</a>, <a href="/wiki/1955_Davis_Cup" title="1955 Davis Cup">1955</a>, <a href="/wiki/1956_Davis_Cup" title="1956 Davis Cup">1956</a>, <a href="/wiki/1957_Davis_Cup" title="1957 Davis Cup">1957</a>, <a href="/wiki/1959_Davis_Cup" title="1959 Davis Cup">1959</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_Davis_Cup" title="1960 Davis Cup">1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961_Davis_Cup" title="1961 Davis Cup">1961</a>, <a href="/wiki/1962_Davis_Cup" title="1962 Davis Cup">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_Davis_Cup" title="1964 Davis Cup">1964</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965_Davis_Cup" title="1965 Davis Cup">1965</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_Davis_Cup" title="1966 Davis Cup">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_Davis_Cup" title="1967 Davis Cup">1967</a>)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Youngest player</b><sup id="cite_ref-records_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-24">[24]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Marco_De_Rossi" title="Marco De Rossi">Marco De Rossi</a>; <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Davis_Cup_team" title="San Marino Davis Cup team">San Marino</a>; 13 years, 319 days (12 May 2011)<sup>1</sup></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Oldest player</b><sup id="cite_ref-records_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-24">[24]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vittorio_Pellandra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vittorio Pellandra (page does not exist)">Vittorio Pellandra</a>; <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Davis_Cup_team" title="San Marino Davis Cup team">San Marino</a>; 66 years, 104 days (11 May 2007)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most years played</b> 
        <ul>
         <li>28, <a href="/wiki/Leander_Paes" title="Leander Paes">Leander Paes</a>, <a href="/wiki/India_Davis_Cup_team" title="India Davis Cup team">India</a> (1990–2018)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most ties played</b><sup id="cite_ref-records_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-24">[24]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li>93, <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Vicini" title="Domenico Vicini">Domenico Vicini</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Davis_Cup_team" title="San Marino Davis Cup team">San Marino</a> (1993–2015)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most rubbers played</b><sup id="cite_ref-records_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-24">[24]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li>164, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Pietrangeli" title="Nicola Pietrangeli">Nicola Pietrangeli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_Davis_Cup_team" title="Italy Davis Cup team">Italy</a> (1954–1972)</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Most rubbers won</b><sup id="cite_ref-records_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-24">[24]</a></sup> 
        <ul>
         <li>Total: 120, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Pietrangeli" title="Nicola Pietrangeli">Nicola Pietrangeli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_Davis_Cup_team" title="Italy Davis Cup team">Italy</a></li> 
         <li>Singles: 78, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Pietrangeli" title="Nicola Pietrangeli">Nicola Pietrangeli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_Davis_Cup_team" title="Italy Davis Cup team">Italy</a></li> 
         <li>Doubles: 43, <a href="/wiki/Leander_Paes" title="Leander Paes">Leander Paes</a>, <a href="/wiki/India_Davis_Cup_team" title="India Davis Cup team">India</a></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <p>The Davis Cup World Group and World Group Play-Off matches awarded <a href="/wiki/ATP_Ranking" class="mw-redirect" title="ATP Ranking">ATP Ranking</a> points from 2009 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Glossary
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>Only live matches earn points; <a href="/wiki/Dead_rubber" title="Dead rubber">dead rubbers</a> earn no points. If a player does not compete in the singles of one or more rounds he will receive points from the previous round when playing singles at the next tie. This last rule also applies for playing in doubles matches.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup>1</sup> A player who wins a singles rubber in the first day of the tie is awarded 5 points, whereas a singles rubber win in tie's last day grants 10 points for a total of 15 available points.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup>2</sup> For the first round only, any player who competes in a live rubber, without a win, receives 10 ranking points for participation.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup>3</sup> Team bonus awarded to a singles player who wins 7 live matches in a calendar year and his team wins the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup>4</sup> Performance bonus awarded to a singles player who wins 8 live matches in a calendar year. In this case, no Team bonus is awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup>5</sup> Team bonus awarded to an unchanged doubles team who wins 4 matches in a calendar year and his team wins the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-ATPRuleBook_58-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATPRuleBook-58">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Davis_Cup_champions" title="List of Davis Cup champions">List of Davis Cup champions</a></li>

       <li><a href="/wiki/History_of_tennis" title="History of tennis">History of tennis</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Davis_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Australasia, British Isles, Caribbean/West Indies, Czechoslovakia, Fiji, Hawaii, Netherlands Antilles, Serbia and Montenegro(SCG)/FR Yugoslavia, Soviet Union/CIS, Yugoslavia SFR.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since 1972, when Challenge Round was abolished. 1st round of Inter-Zonal Zone is considered semi-final round.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Walkover (W.O.) is not counted as win/loss.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-wg-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-wg_29-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-wg_29-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">World Group Play-off ties don't count as World Group ties.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Between 1981 and 1988 winners of zonal finals were directly promoted in World Group while losers in first round of World Group played relegation play-off. That zonal final ties which decided which team is promoted and relegation play-off ties are counted in this statistic.<br>W.O. is not counted.<br>Cuba, Israel and Morocco, each once, were promoted in World Group due to w.o.<br>This ties don't count as World Group ties.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Caribbean/West Indies Davis Cup team until 1987 and Eastern Caribbean Davis Cup team from 1991-96.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-auto-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto_32-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Soviet Union (USSR) Davis Cup team until 1991 and Commonwealth of Independent States (CIS) Davis Cup team in 1992.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nations represented: Australia, New Zealand. Australia and New Zealand have always been two separate countries but did compete together under the alias Australasia from 1905-1914. Despite players from New Zealand being eligible to represent Australasia, Tony Wilding would be the only New Zealander to play for the team while it existed. Australian Davis Cup team was born in 1919 and it assumed all the Australasian Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Assumed all the Australasia Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-auto1-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_35-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_35-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_35-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto1_35-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Caribbean/West Indies Davis Cup team until 1987.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-auto2-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-auto2_36-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto2_36-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto2_36-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-auto2_36-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Yugoslavia Davis Cup team until 1990.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Great Britain and Ireland competed as British Isles from 1900-12 before participating separately from 1913.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nations represented: Bahamas, Barbados, Jamaica, Trinidad and Tobago, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Davis_Cup_team" title="Eastern Caribbean Davis Cup team">Eastern Caribbean Davis Cup team</a>. Caribbean/West Indies last competed in Davis Cup in 1987. Since then, the constituent nations have competed in their own right.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Assumed all the Czechoslovakia Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Czechoslovakia Davis Cup team competed from 1921–1992. Since then, the constituent nations have competed in their own right. All records were assumed by the Czech Republic Davis Cup team.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Caribbean/West Indies Davis Cup team until 1987. Nations represented: full members of The Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States (OECS) and associate members whose population does not exceed 200,000: Anguilla, Antigua and Barbuda (until 1996), British Virgin Islands, Dominica, Grenada, Montserrat, Saint Kitts and Nevis, Saint Lucia (until 1997), Saint Vincent and the Grenadines.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Now represented by Pacific Oceania Davis Cup team.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Assumed all the West Germany Davis Cup team records as East Germany never participated in the Davis Cup.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Assumed all the British Isles Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of British Isles from 1900-12 before participating separately from 1913.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Yugoslavia Davis Cup team until 1992, FR Yugoslavia/Serbia and Montenegro Davis Cup team from 1993-2006 and Serbia Davis Cup team in 2007.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Yugoslavia Davis Cup team until 1992 and FR Yugoslavia/Serbia and Montenegro Davis Cup team from 1993-2006.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dissolved in 2011.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Australasian Davis Cup team until 1914.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nations represented: American Samoa, Cook Islands, Fiji, Guam, Kiribati, Marshall Islands, Federated States of Micronesia, Nauru, Norfolk Island, Northern Mariana Islands, Palau, Papua New Guinea, Samoa, Solomon Islands, Tahiti, Tonga, Tuvalu, Vanuatu.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Assumed all the Soviet Union (USSR) Davis Cup team &amp; CIS Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Caribbean/West Indies Davis Cup team until 1987 and Eastern Caribbean Davis Cup team from 1991-97.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Yugoslavia Davis Cup team until 1992 and FR Yugoslavia/Serbia and Montenegro Davis Cup team from 1993-2006. Assumed all the FR Yugoslavia/Serbia and Montenegro Davis Cup team records.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Competed as part of Yugoslavia Davis Cup team until 1992. Competed as FR Yugoslavia Davis Cup team from 1995-2003 and Serbia and Montenegro (SCG) Davis Cup team from 2004-2006. All records were assumed by the Serbia Davis Cup team.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nations represented: Armenia, Azerbaijan, Belarus, Estonia, Georgia, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Latvia, Lithuania, Moldova, Russia, Tajikistan, Turkmenistan, Ukraine, Uzbekistan. Soviet Union (USSR) Davis Cup team competed from 1962-1991. The team competed as the Commonwealth of Independent States (CIS) in 1992. Since then, the constituent nations have competed in their own right. All records were assumed by the Russia Davis Cup team.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nations represented: Bosnia and Herzegovina, Croatia, Kosovo, Macedonia, Montenegro, Serbia, Slovenia. Yugoslavia last competed in Davis Cup in 1990. Since then, the constituent nations have competed in their own right.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-57">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes all of Rhodesia Davis Cup team records. Rhodesia made 6 Davis Cup appearances between 1963 and 1976.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
